</p>
1,389 km<sup>3</sup>/a (44,000 m<sup>3</sup>/s)</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-header" colspan="2" style="background-color: #CEDEFF;">Basin features</th></tr><tr style="padding: 0 0.6em 0.2em 0.6em;line-height: 1.2em;"><th class="infobox-label" href="/wiki/Gomti_River" title="Gomti River">Gomti</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghaghara_River" title="Ghaghara River">Ghaghara</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gandak_River" <p><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1073938472">.mw-parser-output .geo-default,.mw-parser-output .geo-dms,.mw-parser-output .geo-dec{display:inline}.mw-parser-output .geo-nondefault,.mw-parser-output .geo-multi-punct{display:none}.mw-parser-output .longitude,.mw-parser-output .latitude{white-space:nowrap}</style><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Ganges&amp;params=25.3_N_83.01_E_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">25°18′N</span> <span class="longitude">83°01′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">25.30°N 83.01°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">25.30; 83.01</span></span></span></a></span></span></span>
</p><p>The <b>Ganges</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/dʒ/: 'j' in 'jam'">dʒ</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">GAN</span>-jeez</i></a>) (in India: <b>Ganga</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ʌ/: 'u' in 'cut'">ʌ</span><span title="/ŋ/: 'ng' in 'sing'">ŋ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">GUNG</span>-ə</i></a>); in <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>: <b>Padma</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ʌ/: 'u' in 'cut'">ʌ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">PUD</span>-mə</i></a>))<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-salman-uprety_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-salman-uprety-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swain-ganges_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-swain-ganges-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCGN-Ganges_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-PCGN-Ganges-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uslcsh34-ganges_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-uslcsh34-ganges-8">[8]</a></sup> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-boundary_river" title="Trans-boundary river">trans-boundary river</a> of Asia which flows through <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>. The 2,704 km (1,680 mi) river rises in the western <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> in the Indian <a href="/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India" title="States and union territories of India">state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand" title="Uttarakhand">Uttarakhand</a>. It flows south and east through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gangetic_Plain" title="Gangetic Plain">Gangetic plain</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">North India</a>, receiving the right-bank tributary, the <a href="/wiki/Yamuna" title="Yamuna">Yamuna</a>, which also rises in the western Indian Himalayas, and several left-bank tributaries from <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> that account for the bulk of its flow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swain-ganges-2_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-swain-ganges-2-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> state, India, a feeder canal taking off from its right bank diverts 50% of its flow southwards, artificially connecting it to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hooghly_river" title="Hooghly river">Hooghly river</a>.  The Ganges continues into Bangladesh, its name changing to the <a href="/wiki/Padma_River" title="Padma River">Padma</a>. It is then joined by the <a href="/wiki/Jamuna_River_(Bangladesh)" title="Jamuna River (Bangladesh)">Jamuna</a>, the lower stream of the <a href="/wiki/Brahmaputra_River" title="Brahmaputra River">Brahmaputra</a>, and eventually the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meghna_river" title="Meghna river">Meghna</a>, forming the major estuary of the <a href="/wiki/Ganges_Delta" title="Ganges Delta">Ganges Delta</a>, and emptying into the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>. The Ganges-Brahmaputra-Meghna system is the third largest river on earth <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_by_discharge" title="List of rivers by discharge">by discharge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Main_stem" title="Main stem">main stem</a> of the Ganges begins at the town of <a href="/wiki/Devprayag" title="Devprayag">Devprayag</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ganges-britannica_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-ganges-britannica-1">[1]</a></sup> at the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Alaknanda_River" title="Alaknanda River">Alaknanda</a>, which is the <a href="/wiki/River_source" title="River source">source stream</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hydrology" title="Hydrology">hydrology</a> on account of its greater length, and the <a href="/wiki/Bhagirathi_River" title="Bhagirathi River">Bhagirathi</a>, which is considered the source stream in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> mythology.
</p><p>The Ganges is a lifeline to millions of people who live in its basin and depend on it for their daily needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> It has been important historically, with many former provincial or imperial capitals such as <a href="/wiki/Pataliputra" title="Pataliputra">Pataliputra</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghosh_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ghosh-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kannauj" title="Kannauj">Kannauj</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghosh_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ghosh-14">[14]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kara_(Kaushambi)" title="Kara (Kaushambi)">Kara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munger" title="Munger">Munger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Kashi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hajipur" title="Hajipur">Hajipur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhagalpur" title="Bhagalpur">Bhagalpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murshidabad" title="Murshidabad">Murshidabad</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baharampur" title="Baharampur">Baharampur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kampilya" title="Kampilya">Kampilya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a> located on its banks or the banks of tributaries and connected waterways. The river is home to approximately 140 species of fish, 90 species of <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a>, and also <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptiles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a>, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a> species such as the <a href="/wiki/Gharial" title="Gharial">gharial</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_river_dolphin" title="South Asian river dolphin">South Asian river dolphin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice2012_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice2012-15">[15]</a></sup> The Ganges is the most sacred river to <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alter2001_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alter2001-16">[16]</a></sup> It is worshipped as the goddess <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ganga_in_Hinduism" title="Ganga in Hinduism">Ganga</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BhattacharjiBandyopadhyay1995_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-BhattacharjiBandyopadhyay1995-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Ganges is threatened by <a href="/wiki/Pollution_of_the_Ganges" title="Pollution of the Ganges">severe pollution</a>. This poses a danger not only to humans but also to animals. The levels of <a href="/wiki/Fecal_coliform" title="Fecal coliform">fecal coliform</a> bacteria from human waste in the river near Varanasi are more than a hundred times the Indian government's official limit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice2012_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rice2012-15">[15]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ganga_Action_Plan" title="Ganga Action Plan">Ganga Action Plan</a>, an environmental initiative to clean up the river, has been considered a failure<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haberman_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-haberman-18">[a]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gardner_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-gardner-19">[b]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cleanperish_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-cleanperish-20">[18]</a></sup> which is variously attributed to <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a>, a lack of will in the government, poor technical expertise,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sheth_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-sheth-21">[c]</a></sup> environmental planning<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singh_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-singh-22">[d]</a></sup> and a lack of support from  religious authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-puttick_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-puttick-23">[e]</a></sup>
</p>
